# Dilithium

# Introduction

The purpose of this document is to give a developer all the knowledge necessary to create a GUI for the Dilithium CC Module. We will touch briefly on the usecases of this cryptocondition. This document will not be discussing the underlying math and principles, rather the implementation.

The Dilithium CC allows for quantum resistant transactions on any Komodo assetchain that supports it. It has the added feature of unique human readable handles. These handles can be thought of as an address. For example, instead of a user saying "Please send coins to RD6GgnrMpPaTSMn8vai6yiGA7mN4QGPVMY", they could instead say "Please send coins to my handle, KomodoHaxor". After coins are sent to this unique handle, only the person who registered it, will be able to spend the coins.

The Dilithium CC is a similar concept to Zcash's "z address" or "z transactions", in that there are multiple protocols interacting on the same chain. In the case of Dilithium, the added functionality of this subset of coins is not privacy, rather quantum resistance. Dilithium has "q addresses"(handles) and "q transactions". If we say, "send coins t->q" this is similar to someone saying "send coins t->z" on Zcash.

In order for an assetchain to support it, the Dilithium cclib module must be activated on the chain. Currently, the Dilithium CC is part of the Soduku cclib module. This is a matter of convenience for the developers and testers. It can be separated from the other features in this module if so desired. Please contact us via Discord if you need assitance implementing this CC module into your assetchain.

# Installation

Throughout this document, we will use the test chain, MUSIG. Replace MUSIG with the relevant ticker for your chain in any komodo-cli commands. This is also a test chain for the Musig CC module. The Musig CC is an entirely seperate set of functionality. Do not conflate the two. Dilithium testing is being done on this chain as a matter of convenience for the developers and testers.

./komodod -ac_name=MUSIG -ac_supply=100000 -ac_reward=10000000 -ac_cclib=sudoku -ac_cc=2 -addnode=5.9.102.210 -addnode=195.201.20.230 -addnode=195.201.137.5

Please follow Installing Komodo Manually, if you have not done this already. Please note, that the process is different because we are using a custom cclib module that is not typically included in the Komodo Daemon(komodod) unless komodod is explictily built for this module. Follow the above guide, once you finish the ./zcutil/build.sh step, do this:

cd ~/komodo/src/cc
./makecclib
cp sudoku.so ../libcc.so
cd ../..
make

# General flow of the Dilithium CC Module

  1. User registers a handle with the keypair and register commands.

  2. The handle is then funded with the Qsend (q->q) or send (t->q) commands.

  3. User can then send coins within the q pool(q->q) or send coins from the q pool back to a normal R address or p2sk address(q->t) with the Qsend command.

We will begin by going through the manual process of creating a handle, sending coins to this handle then sending coins from this handle. After going through the manual process, we will show some code examples of how this might be implemented into a UI. A TUI with Dilithium functionality can be found here.

# Walkthrough

# Step 1: Start the daemon with a pubkey and backup its privkey

Start the komodod, by setting -pubkey= in the launch parameters. See Launching with pubkey to learn about obtaining a pubkey.

./komodod -ac_name=MUSIG -ac_supply=100000 -ac_reward=10000000 -ac_cclib=sudoku -ac_cc=2 -addnode=5.9.102.210 -addnode=195.201.20.230 -addnode=195.201.137.5 -pubkey=0377ffe2b64443ac5e746f29b021e22411c7731d675f169d32423f8f3d6fc9ea3b

# Note

If the chain you're using has the ac_pubkey parameter, you must not change the -ac_pubkey= value. Do not confuse -pubkey= with -ac_pubkey=. These are entirely seperate parameters.

To check that the pubkey is set properly, do:

./komodo-cli -ac_name=MUSIG setpubkey

{
  "error": "Can only set pubkey once, to change it you need to restart your daemon.",
  "address": "RVXJpc9N4j35psbqmRZzgpKmo98w1CnvHA",
  "pubkey": "0377ffe2b64443ac5e746f29b021e22411c7731d675f169d32423f8f3d6fc9ea3b"
}

If this does not output the -pubkey= value and corresponding address, you have not set it properly.

It is important to backup the private key for this -pubkey= address. Without it, any handles registered with it will not be accessible.

# Step 2: Create a Dilithium keypair using a random string

Run the following commands in your terminal.

./komodo-cli -ac_name=MUSIG cclib keypair 19 "[%22rand%22]"

Learn about the %22s in the command here: CC Lib Formatting

This command generates a Dilithium keypair using a random seed.

  "pkaddr": "PMrTr4qgErBbDkwxuSdfRNXkrSMoxbhb2R",
  "skaddr": "ScrFviWo9jaJdi7EHz3w2tX1xhvHR8e9Kb",
  "result": "success"
}
  • The "seed" and "privkey" values are sensitive information and need to be stored securely.
  • The "pubkey" and "privkey" values are simply the Dilithium keypair.
  • The "pkaddr" and "skaddr" values are a hashed representation of the Dilithium pubkey and Dilithium privkey. These *kaddr values aren't neccesary for functionality. They are included as an easy way to compare Dilithium pubkeys and privkeys.
  • At a minimum, the "seed" value should be saved. For simplicity, it's best to save the full output of this command. Wherever this is saved, treat it as a sensitive file, similar to a wallet.dat. Later in this document, we will touch upon what information must be saved and how you might structure this data.

# Step 3: Check whether a handle is available

We can use the handleinfo rpc command to check whether a handle is available.

./komodo-cli -ac_name=MUSIG cclib handleinfo 19 "[%22KomodoHaxor%22]"

{
  "result": "success",
  "handle": "KomodoHaxor",
  "status": "available"
}

# Step 3: Register a handle that is available

We can now use the "seed" value to register the handle.

./komodo-cli -ac_name=MUSIG cclib register 19 "[%22KomodoHaxor%22,%22e580f34e9bdfd23108409e76475c7df3f924d149d494d5cdbc24aeb280237d4a%22]"

The "hex" value here is a signed raw transaction. We now need to broadcast it.

d60d224d7855a40507064c5ca72ed7d84a54340174eb16e31d079e4b4f230940

If we now check handleinfo again, we see that we have successfully registered the handle:

./komodo-cli -ac_name=MUSIG cclib handleinfo 19 "[%22KomodoHaxor%22]"

{
  "result": "success",
  "handle": "KomodoHaxor",
  "destpubtxid": "d60d224d7855a40507064c5ca72ed7d84a54340174eb16e31d079e4b4f230940",
  "pkaddr": "PMrTr4qgErBbDkwxuSdfRNXkrSMoxbhb2R",
  "pubkey": "0377ffe2b64443ac5e746f29b021e22411c7731d675f169d32423f8f3d6fc9ea3b"
}

# Note

The "destpubtxid" value here can be thought of as the Dilithium address. The handle and -pubkey= address used to register it are tied to this Dilithium public key, PMrTr4qgErBbDkwxuSdfRNXkrSMoxbhb2R.

The Dilithium keypair can later be changed. Currently, the -pubkey= address associated with the handle cannot be changed.

# Step 4: Send some coins to the registered handle

Now we can send some coins t->q using the send rpc command. The paramters must be <handle>,<destpubtxid>,<amount>.

./komodo-cli -ac_name=MUSIG cclib send 19 "[%22KomodoHaxor%22,%22d60d224d7855a40507064c5ca72ed7d84a54340174eb16e31d079e4b4f230940%22,7.77]"

{
  "handle": "KomodoHaxor",
  "hex": "0400008085202f89014009234f4b9e071de316eb740134544ad8d72ea75c4c060705a455784d220dd604000000494830450221008e7c4905498d2cf1597e044dbc79a489ce48c81c5ca421b98e84f4158d876b1c022024901a2862245685fe16ab865a49c9ea939bfed7ea5a9a71d7ac12f84d42be9501ffffffff034014502e00000000302ea22c80200c0396b7e2db09ab239f0b337fbc7df888273e60323a63d0caa862116bcf51a48103120c008203000401cc8052c51f0200000023210377ffe2b64443ac5e746f29b021e22411c7731d675f169d32423f8f3d6fc9ea3bac0000000000000000246a2213784009234f4b9e071de316eb740134544ad8d72ea75c4c060705a455784d220dd600000000936c00000000000000000000000000",
  "txid": "c314304cecded6cd593daeddf676b2a8c424a604f973e68e6777b84e39ef8548",
  "result": "success"
}

Now broadcast this transaction.

./komodo-cli -ac_name=MUSIG sendrawtransaction 0400008085202f89014009234f4b9e071de316eb740134544ad8d72ea75c4c060705a455784d220dd604000000494830450221008e7c4905498d2cf1597e044dbc79a489ce48c81c5ca421b98e84f4158d876b1c022024901a2862245685fe16ab865a49c9ea939bfed7ea5a9a71d7ac12f84d42be9501ffffffff034014502e00000000302ea22c80200c0396b7e2db09ab239f0b337fbc7df888273e60323a63d0caa862116bcf51a48103120c008203000401cc8052c51f0200000023210377ffe2b64443ac5e746f29b021e22411c7731d675f169d32423f8f3d6fc9ea3bac0000000000000000246a2213784009234f4b9e071de316eb740134544ad8d72ea75c4c060705a455784d220dd600000000936c00000000000000000000000000

c314304cecded6cd593daeddf676b2a8c424a604f973e68e6777b84e39ef8548

Later in this document we will discuss how to get the balance for a given handle, but for now we know our handle, KomodoHaxor, has 1 qUTXO with a value of 7.77 coins.

You can specify outputs of a Qsend transaction by either the ScriptPubKey for a given R address or the destpubtxid for a given Dilithium handle.

# Step 5: Send some coins from one handle to another handle

  • In this example we will be sending 0.1 coins to the handle "KomodoFan". Assume this handle already exists i.e., registered on the blockchain
  • This is a q->q transaction using the Qsend RPC
  • We must first obtain the destpubtxid for this handle.
./komodo-cli -ac_name=MUSIG cclib handleinfo 19 "[%22KomodoFan%22]"

{
  "result": "success",
  "handle": "KomodoFan",
  "destpubtxid": "af710c0fd6aeb54556ee401803bc4cc39ea9002ad5228f308b27eb3af0e4c4b6",
  "pkaddr": "PRZniLRiLY5Laoqbg7CjQSktX34x99jdCp",
  "pubkey": "03cebc558e6ba1c0f56f4ad490391c93336b5ccd8b08d123f4e7f1cdd4d5d21e61"
}

The first two arguments neccesary for the Qsend rpc command are "destpubtxid" and "seed" values of the handle that is sending coins. We will refer to this "destpubtxid" value as "mypubtxid" in the following examples. The remaining arguments will specify each output of the transaction. The inputs will be chosen automatically. A Dilithium change output will be created automatically. This change output will send the remaining coins back to "mypubtxid".

./komodo-cli -ac_name=MUSIG cclib Qsend 19 "[%22d60d224d7855a40507064c5ca72ed7d84a54340174eb16e31d079e4b4f230940%22,%22e580f34e9bdfd23108409e76475c7df3f924d149d494d5cdbc24aeb280237d4a%22,%22af710c0fd6aeb54556ee401803bc4cc39ea9002ad5228f308b27eb3af0e4c4b6%22,0.1]"

{
  "hex": }

In vout0, we have the 0.1 coins we sent to the KomodoFan handle. We see this address, RGBrSwrGR4ypFFufyvHEuMMbxs7ETD8Xv7. This is the CC address for the node that created the KomodoFan handle.

# Note

Every address has a unique CC address for each CC. This CC address is unique to this node and this module. All handles created using the same -pubkey= address will store their UTXOs in their own CC address. This means that all handles registered from the same -pubkey= address will use this same CC address.

We can use the cclibaddress command to check that this is indeed KomodoFan's CC address. We will use the pubkey shown from the cclib handleinfo 19 "[%22KomodoFan%22]" command we executed previously.

./komodo-cli -ac_name=MUSIG cclibaddress 19 03cebc558e6ba1c0f56f4ad490391c93336b5ccd8b08d123f4e7f1cdd4d5d21e61

3e8cb40dce149297a4c91d8606b209db1ef3d2eb81ca93f6bbb575d503e947db43e249c8bb3da821d3084fba79a97566903ea1f91748a964944d9df963f6159cc0f2d980c437b816915b5a184b78b494710b6602a29a26f6ef7863e86a99278a598ce715f558777c8c63b83931fa95d453d89642e954db65599771612d0cd6b46fbaa0ccd7b815908e789e35fd670e83331facee77715056cf89a53ed1b04a6f15c34a2db2a47a0ef4c96d9e08c4a1ed7714a59ad82704e973bd099841f6c4e7c38017263d8d6aac7532307735a872af278108cac7856a40d8807a7f7bdce715b5ec3d2cbfef14767dc30c9fb5ceee7177bd3ff42fd1386a2e01f3de4c31b9537040ef13fb1f8b365a7ced2a6afd5914208bfe17cfa160f4f4b5bc436ca65adfb2c3f7f51838f9dcc9f3516f7668a211d37855b203d2011eb50d7b5c5dc4da2e0026a52c0f05b325b84b7fb2080889f7e9a2ce07ba6a6ba5e3f7e088ee1aefd6fed67a79656305443074a3d45316a4ab0a6382ca625c69c3518c1bc3998a078b7b225700226d692711c0a5340ea1782673dbdccc51288e24350544bf3a329aef666fbc78f087f8fbdb5abbcdae5194103cb7d00adbcec6dd9324e408b1657324650b2e98e8ed5da0543fb8e26ea4270d46fdd60d224d7855a40507064c5ca72ed7d84a54340174eb16e31d079e4b4f23094051130dac4d6a
  • Right away you can see the destpubtxid for the KomodoHaxor handle, d60d224d7855a40507064c5ca72ed7d84a54340174eb16e31d079e4b4f230940.
  • Followed by that you see the destpubtxid for KomodoFan, af710c0fd6aeb54556ee401803bc4cc39ea9002ad5228f308b27eb3af0e4c4b6.
  • This indicates that vout0 was sent to the KomodoFan handle and that vout1 was sent to the KomodoHaxor handle. Since we know there are 2 vouts other than the OP_RETURN in this transaction, we know that vout1 will be at [:64] and that vout0 will be at [64:128].
  • We again see KomodoHaxor's destpubtxid, d60d224d7855a40507064c5ca72ed7d84a54340174eb16e31d079e4b4f230940 at [-76:-12].
  • This indicates the destpubtxid of the inputs. The destpubtxid of the sender will always be the same position in a Qsend transaction's OP_RETURN, [-76:-12].

# Step 7: A more complex Qsend

Let's move to a more complex Qsend. We will now send a Qsend transaction with outputs to multiple R addresses and multiple Dilithium handles.

  • We'll send KomodoHaxor's 7.6699 coin qUTXO from the previous transaction.
  • We will send 1 coin to KomodoFan, 1.1 coins to the handle LABSLover and 1.2 coins to RRyyejME7LRTuvdziWsXkAbSW1fdiohGwK. We will also send 1.3 coins to bKnMWGuXC5HEyxk3GttsT1a9TtYWKbBpEP, a multisig address, to demonstrate that this will work with any script hash.
  • There is one limitation to the above rule: Any 32 byte hex string is interpretted as a Dilithium destpubtxid.
  • This means a 32 byte "scriptPubKey" value doesn't work.

This transaction will automatically send the change back to our handle, KomodoHaxor. We first need to obtain the destpubtxids for any handles we will be sending to or the ScriptPubKey for any R addresses we will be sending to.

We will use the handleinfo rpc command to obtain the destpubtxid for the LABSLover handle. We know the destpubtxid for KomodoFan from the previous step.

./komodo-cli -ac_name=MUSIG cclib handleinfo 19 "[%22LABSLover%22]"

{
  "result": "success",
  "handle": "LABSLover",
  "destpubtxid": "b625e38064cb0c940a55f0dca7e6b60270aac090d0dd90d4e43e924d696564a2",
  "pkaddr": "P8bX1ddLLaR149rZZEXkWTAbLTgczsM4vK",
  "pubkey": "03cebc558e6ba1c0f56f4ad490391c93336b5ccd8b08d123f4e7f1cdd4d5d21e61"
}

We can use the validateaddress rpc command to obtain the "scriptPubKey value for both RRyyejME7LRTuvdziWsXkAbSW1fdiohGwK and bKnMWGuXC5HEyxk3GttsT1a9TtYWKbBpEP.

./komodo-cli -ac_name=MUSIG validateaddress RRyyejME7LRTuvdziWsXkAbSW1fdiohGwK

{
  "isvalid": true,
  "address": "RRyyejME7LRTuvdziWsXkAbSW1fdiohGwK",
  "scriptPubKey": "76a914b738b1730cfb58960b1dd1765c6d3276993959e188ac",
  "segid": 13,
  "ismine": false,
  "iswatchonly": false,
  "isscript": false
}

./komodo-cli -ac_name=MUSIG validateaddress bKnMWGuXC5HEyxk3GttsT1a9TtYWKbBpEP

{
  "isvalid": true,
  "address": "bKnMWGuXC5HEyxk3GttsT1a9TtYWKbBpEP",
  "scriptPubKey": "a9144d5e24fcd799f3a3fa15f98a6c69a5829596f56087",
  "segid": 26,
  "ismine": false,
  "iswatchonly": false,
  "isscript": true
}

./komodo-cli -ac_name=MUSIG cclib Qsend 19 "[%22d60d224d7855a40507064c5ca72ed7d84a54340174eb16e31d079e4b4f230940%22,%22e580f34e9bdfd23108409e76475c7df3f924d149d494d5cdbc24aeb280237d4a%22,%22af710c0fd6aeb54556ee401803bc4cc39ea9002ad5228f308b27eb3af0e4c4b6%22,1,%22b625e38064cb0c940a55f0dca7e6b60270aac090d0dd90d4e43e924d696564a2%22,1.1,%2276a914b738b1730cfb58960b1dd1765c6d3276993959e188ac%22,1.2,%22a9144d5e24fcd799f3a3fa15f98a6c69a5829596f56087%22,1.3]"

  • If we look at position [:64], we will see destpubtxid for vout 4, d60d224d7855a40507064c5ca72ed7d84a54340174eb16e31d079e4b4f230940.
  • We see that [64:128] is null bytes. This is because vout 3 is to a normal address, not a Dilithium handle.
  • We see that [128:192] is also null bytes. [128:192] is vout 2.
  • [192:256], b625e38064cb0c940a55f0dca7e6b60270aac090d0dd90d4e43e924d696564a2, is the destpubtxid for the LABSLover handle.
  • [256:320], af710c0fd6aeb54556ee401803bc4cc39ea9002ad5228f308b27eb3af0e4c4b6, is the destpubtxid for the KomodoFan handle.
  • Finally we see that once again, the sender's destpubtxid, d60d224d7855a40507064c5ca72ed7d84a54340174eb16e31d079e4b4f230940 is at [-76:-12].

# Step 9: Finding the balance for a given handle

We can now look at how we can find the balance for a given handle. We will go over how to do q_listunspent for an arbitary handle. We will use the LABSLover handle in this example.

We need to first get the CC address associated with this handle. We will do this by using the handleinfo and cclibaddress rpc commands.

./komodo-cli -ac_name=MUSIG cclib handleinfo 19 "[%22LABSLover%22]"

{
  "result": "success",
  "handle": "LABSLover",
  "destpubtxid": "b625e38064cb0c940a55f0dca7e6b60270aac090d0dd90d4e43e924d696564a2",
  "pkaddr": "P8bX1ddLLaR149rZZEXkWTAbLTgczsM4vK",
  "pubkey": "03cebc558e6ba1c0f56f4ad490391c93336b5ccd8b08d123f4e7f1cdd4d5d21e61"
}

We can now use this "pubkey" value with the cclibaddress rpc command.

./komodo-cli -ac_name=MUSIG cclibaddress 19 03cebc558e6ba1c0f56f4ad490391c93336b5ccd8b08d123f4e7f1cdd4d5d21e61

{
  "result": "success",
  "CClibCCAddress": "RJxChTpGrT8Y64NxTK95TVs3r8wPCwswKF",
  "CClibCCBalance": 0.01,
  "CClibNormalAddress": "RCUDfxQCgXpB8bKqkzwBrR4cG8HxjAzJ7Y",
  "CClibNormalBalance": 0.0,

This CC address may have multiple Dilithium handles associated with it. We cannot assume all of these UTXOs belong to the LABSLover handle. This is where some coding will come into play. We will need to iterate over each of these UTXOs, check if it's either a Dilithium send transaction or Dilithium Qsend transaction, if it is, check if it belongs to the LABSLover handle. Generally any UTXO with a value of 0.0001 coins can be ignored. These are created by the Dilithium register rpc command. They are used to index handles for a given pubkey.

Let's look at this UTXO and find out if it's a Dilithium UTXO. If it is, we will go through how to find out the associated handle.

{
  "address": "RGBrSwrGR4ypFFufyvHEuMMbxs7ETD8Xv7",
  "txid": "5b5dab18abbfc0b85c6632ec6b4f71e30d7e28cbfa5e29a6a6e4d48f2fb730cf",
  "outputIndex": 0,
  "script": "2ea22c802008b4a3a211fa1ecb9d245b3267827a56924653fe9bb4697510cf5d65e4bbfea98103120c008203000401cc",
  "satoshis": 100000000,
  "height": 25034
}

Use the getrawtransaction rpc command on this "txid" value.

./komodo-cli -ac_name=MUSIG getrawtransaction 5b5dab18abbfc0b85c6632ec6b4f71e30d7e28cbfa5e29a6a6e4d48f2fb730cf 2

{
  "result": "success",
  "OpRets": [
    {
      "eval_code": "0x13",
      "function": "Q"
    }
  ]
}
  • The "eval_code" value here is the eval code for the Dilithium CC module. All transactions created using the Dilithium CC module will use this same eval code. This eval code is defined in the CC's code.
  • The "function" is the function id for Dilithium Qsend transactions. Each CC module will have a function id for each unique transaction type it has. These values can be found for a given CC module using the cclibinfo rpc command.
./komodo-cli -ac_name=MUSIG cclibinfo

  • Here we see that the eval code for Dilithium is 19 or 0x13 in hex. We also see that the function id for the Qsend method is "Q". Again, ignore anything related to Musig, Soduku or faucet2. These are part of this cclib module as a matter of convenience for the developers and testers. We will discuss each of the Dilithium methods later in this document.

Now that we know this is in fact a Dilithium Qsend transaction, let's use the same process as before to get the destpubtxid of the inputs and the destpubtxids of the outputs. We'll start by converting the OP_RETURN's "hex" value to big endian.

  • We know this transaction has two outputs other than the OP_RETURN transaction. This means that the Dilithium handle's destpubtxid for vout1 will be [:64] and that the destpubtixd for vout0 will be [64:128].
  • If we look at each of these positions, we will see that we have adebadd9483bb3d6edd10304dc162506a36adc4aabb14dd13a623042f339236d for vout 1. We have fc6c067ec1091ec0d57ab86812af85a8650b10c6f1f0b954fc8db8c0e877e2a9 for vout 0.
  • Neither of these match LABSLover's destpubtxid, so this UTXO does not belong to the LABSLover handle. - To find out which handles these do belong to, we can use this python function to determine the handle.

Please note, this we will be using python3 for the rest of this guide. This will work with any language that can interact with the daemon via rpc. We will be using the slickrpc library to interact with the daemon.

Learn how to use the slickrpc library here.

# function to get handle from register txid
def handle_get(register_txid, rpc_connection):
        tx = rpc_connection.getrawtransaction(register_txid, 1)
        OP_ret = tx['vout'][-1]['scriptPubKey']['hex']
        byte_length = OP_ret[12:14]
        byte_length_int = int(byte_length, 16)
        x = (byte_length_int * 2) + 14
        return(bytes.fromhex(OP_ret[14:x]).decode('utf-8'))

We first need to get the OP_RETURN for this destpubtxid , adebadd9483bb3d6edd10304dc162506a36adc4aabb14dd13a623042f339236d.

./komodo-cli -ac_name=MUSIG getrawtransaction adebadd9483bb3d6edd10304dc162506a36adc4aabb14dd13a623042f339236d 2

      "type": "nulldata"
    }

]
  • If we look at the position, [12:14], of this "hex" value, this will tell us the length of the handle.
  • This position will be the same for all destpubtxids.
  • In this case, this byte is 05 . This means that the 5 bytes following this value is the handle in ascii.
  • If we look at following 5 bytes at [14:24], we see 6e65773230. Converting this to text, we get new20.

To see that this is in fact the handle for adebadd9483bb3d6edd10304dc162506a36adc4aabb14dd13a623042f339236d, we can use the handleinfo rpc command.

./komodo-cli -ac_name=MUSIG cclib handleinfo 19 "[%22new20%22]"

{
  "result": "success",
  "handle": "new20",
  "destpubtxid": "adebadd9483bb3d6edd10304dc162506a36adc4aabb14dd13a623042f339236d",
  "pkaddr": "PPYtLWAwewUY1TNwsHyJpo7GdFLgrZcf5t",
  "pubkey": "03cebc558e6ba1c0f56f4ad490391c93336b5ccd8b08d123f4e7f1cdd4d5d21e61"
}
  • If we repeat the same process for the remining destpubtxid, fc6c067ec1091ec0d57ab86812af85a8650b10c6f1f0b954fc8db8c0e877e2a9. We find that the output is to the new21 handle.
  • We will need to repeat this process on each UTXO in the getaddressesutxos output. Please see the dil_listunspent function here for how you might do this in python3.

If we use the decodeccopret rpc command on this transaction's OP_RETURN "hex" value, we can see that this is a Dilithium send(t->q) transaction. We know this because the "function" value is "x".

./komodo-cli -ac_name=MUSIG decodeccopret 6a221378a26465694d923ee4d490ddd090c0aa7002b6e6a7dcf0550a940ccb6480e325b6

{
  "result": "success",
  "OpRets": [
    {
      "eval_code": "0x13",
      "function": "x"
    }
  ]

Now, if we convert this "hex" value to big endian, we get:

b625e38064cb0c940a55f0dca7e6b60270aac090d0dd90d4e43e924d696564a27813226a
  • If we take the first 32 bytes of this, or [:64], we get b625e38064cb0c940a55f0dca7e6b60270aac090d0dd90d4e43e924d696564a2.
  • This is the destpubtxid that vout 0 was sent to in this transaction. If we use the handle_get function from the previous step, we find that this destpubtxid is for the handle LABSLover.
  • Looking at the vouts of the qutxo that belong to the handle and adding their balances will give the total balance

# keypair

cclib keypair 19 '["hexseed"]'

The keypair method generates a Dilithium pubkey and privkey when a 256 bit seed in hex format (64 characters) is provided. Else, it creates a new seed and produces the Dilithium pubkey and privkey from it.

# Arguments

Name Type Description
hexseed (string) a random hex to provide entropy for calculating the key pair

# Response

Name Type Description
status (string) the quality of the seed used
seed (string) the seed used (either the provided one if it satisfies the requirements or a seed created by the daemon)
pubkey (string) the Dilithium pubkey generated
privkey (string) the Dilithium privkey generated
pkaddr (string) the hashed representation of the Dilithium pubkey
skaddr (string) the hashed representation of the Dilithium privkey
result (string) whether the call executed successfully

# 📌 Examples

Command:

./komodo-cli -ac_name=MUSIG cclib keypair 19 '["rand"]'

{
  "status": "using random high entropy seed",
  "seed": "a70a8e7d2281beaf0762a11590fb566d7af32325ae4252609149de37658e2eb5",

# register

cclib register 19 '["handle","hexseed"]'

The register method allows a handle be registered to the pubkey running the node using a valid seed from the keypair step.

# Arguments

Name Type Description
handle (string) the desired handle
hexseed (string) the seed used to create the Dilithium keypair

# Response

Name Type Description
handle (string) the handle registered
pkaddr (string) the hashed representation of the Dilithium pubkey
skaddr (string) the hashed representation of the Dilithium privkey
hex (string) the hex that should be broadcast to register the handle
txid (string) the transaction id that will be generated when the hex is broadcasted
result (string) whether the call executed successfully

# 📌 Examples

Command:

./komodo-cli -ac_name=MUSIG cclib register 19 '["AtomicWarrior","a70a8e7d2281beaf0762a11590fb566d7af32325ae4252609149de37658e2eb5"]'

# handleinfo

cclib handleinfo 19 '["handle"]'

The handleinfo method displays the appropriate information related to the handle supplied.

# Arguments

Name Type Description
handle (string) the handle whose information is to be queried

# Response

# When a handle is available
Name Type Description
result (string) whether the call executed successfully
handle (string) the handle whose information is queried
status (string) whether the handle is available

OR

# When a handle is already registered by the node executing the command
Name Type Description
result (string) whether the call executed successfully
handle (string) the handle
destpubtxid (string) the transaction id that was generated when the handle was registered
pkaddr (string) the hashed representation of the Dilithium pubkey
pubkey (string) the pubkey of the node that registered the handle

# 📌 Examples

# When a handle is available
./komodo-cli -ac_name=MUSIG cclib handleinfo 19 '["KomodoHaxor"]'

{
  "result": "success",
  "handle": "KomodoHaxor",
  "status": "available"
}
# When a handle is already registered by the node executing the command

Command:

./komodo-cli -ac_name=MUSIG cclib handleinfo 19 '["AtomicWarrior"]'

{
  "result": "success",
  "handle": "AtomicWarrior",
  "destpubtxid": "ea448ff66aa925239cff7ca748d3aea62474187fefbd1c15fcaaa14c4529b82a",
  "pkaddr": "PCD25oVW6JVzkNgg3MUB21uorh7BDj6TtD",
  "pubkey": "0225f1cbbda1a0c406bb8f6dc7a589d88b2f9e28cd4fdb3f59139f8aff1f5d270a"
}

# sign

cclib sign 19 '["msg","hexseed"]'

The sign method signs a given 32 byte message in the hex format using the Dilithium seed supplied.

# Arguments

Name Type Description
msg (string) the 32 byte hexmessage to be signed
hexseed (string) the seed used to sign the message

# Response

Name Type Description
msg32 (string) the message that has been signed
pkaddr (string) the hashed representation of the Dilithium pubkey
skaddr (string) the hashed representation of the Dilithium privkey
signature (string) the signature generated
sighash (string) the hash of the signature

# 📌 Examples

Command:

./komodo-cli -ac_name=MUSIG cclib sign 19 '["5175616e74756d20526573697374616e636520697320617765736f6d65212121","a70a8e7d2281beaf0762a11590fb566
d7af32325ae4252609149de37658e2eb5"]'

# verify

cclib verify 19 '["pubtxid","msg","sig"]'

The verify method verifies whether the supplied signature has been generated for the message by the seed corresponding to the handle refered by the pubtxid

# Arguments

Name Type Description
pubtxid (string) the id of the handle registration transaction
msg (string) the message that has been signed
sig (string) the signature generated

# Response

Name Type Description
sighash (string) the hash of the signature
msg32 (string) the message that has been signed
handle (string) the handle that was registered with the seed used to sign the message
pkaddr (string) the hashed representation of the Dilithium pubkey corresponding to the seed
result (string) whether the call executed successfully

# 📌 Examples

Command:

./komodo-cli -ac_name=MUSIG cclib verify 19 # send

cclib send 19 '["handle","pubtxid",amount]'

The send method sends the specified amount of coins to a handle refered by the pubtxid

# Arguments

Name Type Description
handle (string) the recipient's handle
pubtxid (string) the id of the handle registration transaction
amount (number) the amount of coins to be sent

# Response

Name Type Description
handle (string) the recipient's handle
hex (string) the transaction hex that should be broadcasted
txid (string) the transaction id that will be generated when the hex is broadcasted
result (string) whether the call executed successfully

# 📌 Examples

Command:

./komodo-cli -ac_name=MUSIG cclib send 19 '["AtomicWarrior","ea448ff66aa925239cff7ca748d3aea62474187fefbd1c15fcaaa14c4529b82a",1]'

# spend

cclib spend 19 '["sendtxid","scriptPubKey","hexseed"]'

The spend method spends the coins recieved in the transaction of id sendtxid to a scriptPubkey using the supplied seed

# Arguments

Name Type Description
sendtxid (string) the id of the transaction that sent coins to the handle associated with the seed supplied
scriptPubKey (string) the scriptPubkey to which the coins are to be spent
hexseed (string) the sees used to register the handle which holds the funds

# Response

Name Type Description
hex (string) the hex that has to be broadcasted
txid (string) the transaction id that will be generated when the hex is broadcasted
result (string) whether the call executed successfully

# 📌 Examples

Command:

./komodo-cli -ac_name=MUSIG cclib spend 19 '["18e3a7c746e8eb7a7e1835e54e46ef6f227fb41c7142bf0304b453c0034b31fb","21029b086d4e3e0358f668ccc3da07df6343fb29970b742f0bc128f180994c5222c1ac","a70a8e7d2281beaf0762a11590fb566d7af32325ae4252609149de37658e2eb5"]'

# Qsend

cclib Qsend 19 '["mypubtxid","hexseed/'mypriv'","destpubtxid1",amount1,"destpubtxid2",amount2,...]

The Qsend method sends coins from the handle on the node to anynumber of other handles refered by their pubtxids. This transaction uses the Dilithium signing and is quantum resistant. Multiple "destpubtxid",amount can be appended to the array to specify multiple recipients.

# Arguments

Name Type Description
mypubtxid (string) the id of the handle registration transaction of the sender
hexseed/'mypriv' (string) the seed used to register the handle
destpubtxid (string) the the id of the handle registration transaction of the recepient
amount (number) the amount of coins to be sent to the handle being refered

# Response

Name Type Description
hex (string) the hex that has to be broadcasted
txid (string) the transaction id that will be generated when the hex is broadcasted
result (string) whether the call executed successfully

# 📌 Examples

Command:

./komodo-cli -ac_name=MUSIG cclib Qsend 19 "[%22d60d224d7855a40507064c5ca72ed7d84a54340174eb16e31d079e4b4f230940%22,%22e580f34e9bdfd23108409e76475c7df3f924d149d494d5cdbc24aeb280237d4a%22,%22af710c0fd6aeb54556ee401803bc4cc39ea9002ad5228f308b27eb3af0e4c4b6%22,1,%22b625e38064cb0c940a55f0dca7e6b60270aac090d0dd90d4e43e924d696564a2%22,1.1,%2276a914b738b1730cfb58960b1dd1765c6d3276993959e188ac%22,1.2,%22a9144d5e24fcd799f3a3fa15f98a6c69a5829596f56087%22,1.3]"
